						<section id="what-is">
				<a href="#" id="hide-what-is">Hide this</a>
				<a href="/about" id="more-what-is">
				<h2>What is Next Nature?</h2>
				<p>With our attempts to cultivate nature, humankind causes the rising of a next nature, which is wild and unpredictable as ever. Wild systems, genetic surprises, autonomous machinery and splendidly beautiful black flowers. Nature changes along with us.</p>
				</a>
			</section>

<div class="list">
	
			<h2>Posts Tagged &#8216;Designed-by-Evolution&#8217;</h2>
	
	<ul id="article-list">	
		
			<li>
				<article id="post-44628">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/05/hacking-human-cells-to-use-solar-power/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="353" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/shutterstock_255109180-530x353.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="shutterstock_255109180" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/05/hacking-human-cells-to-use-solar-power/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Hacking Human Cells to Use Solar Power">Hacking Human Cells to Use Solar Power</a></h2>
					<p>Our cells are not that different from a car engine: they depend on carbon-based fuels for energy. But using carbon for energy is an inefficient process. This is what the biotech startup <a href="http://www.biplastiq.com/" target="_blank">BiPlastiq</a> seeks to resolve, using solar energy instead of carbon and oxygen, by hacking our cells.</p>
<p>The founder of BiPlastiq, Christopher Powell believes that by hacking our mitochondrial structures to use solar energy, the power output of our bodies might increase dramatically. This upgrade could arguably transform human bodies into regenerative machines and extend human lives by decades.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/05/hacking-human-cells-to-use-solar-power/#more-44628" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

			<li>
				<article id="post-44605">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/anthropo-scene-7-anthropocene-bird/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="353" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/IMG_1866-530x353.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="IMG_1866" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/anthropo-scene-7-anthropocene-bird/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Anthropo-scene #7: Anthropocene Bird">Anthropo-scene #7: Anthropocene Bird</a></h2>
					<p>What does it mean to be a bird in a world massively altered by human actions? This White-tailed Kite (Elanus leucurus), a beautiful raptor, is finding it out while hovering above Baylands Park near Palo Alto, California.</p>
<p>Humans have made not only the Dodo, but dozens of bird species, vanish from Earth in the past decades, through hunting, habitat destruction and the spread of cats, rats and dogs with the help of ships. Globally, 1300 out of a total of 10,000 bird species are seriously in decline. Other birds have learned to live with humans and profit from their presence.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/anthropo-scene-7-anthropocene-bird/#more-44605" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

			<li>
				<article id="post-44432">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/plastivore-a-bird-that-feeds-on-plastic/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="420" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/04/plastivore_bird-530x420.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="plastivore_bird" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/plastivore-a-bird-that-feeds-on-plastic/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Plastivore – A Bird that Feeds on Plastic">Plastivore – A Bird that Feeds on Plastic</a></h2>
					<p>Imagine humankind would magically disappear from the planet today. We would leave the ruins of cities, roads, cars and&#8230; plastics. Since its invention in 1907, <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/themes/plastic-planet/" target="_blank">plastic steadily worked its way into the geology of Earth</a>. As plastics hardly break down they could survive humankind.</p>
<p>Artist <a href="http://brittduppen.com/" target="_blank">Britt Duppen</a> envisions that, in due time, new species might evolve that could feed on plastic. Her speculative &#8216;Plastivore&#8217; bird (Latin for ‘plastic eater’, <em>plasticio</em> meaning ‘plastic’ or ‘food that contains particles of plastic’ and <em>vorare</em> meaning ‘to devour’) thrives on a diet of fungi and plastics.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/plastivore-a-bird-that-feeds-on-plastic/#more-44432" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

				<article id="post-44110">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/recreating-woolly-mammoth-dna/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="475" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/03/shutterstock_248386057-530x475.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="shutterstock_248386057" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/recreating-woolly-mammoth-dna/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Recreating Woolly Mammoth DNA">Recreating Woolly Mammoth DNA</a></h2>
					<p>Bioengineering might soon enable us to bring long gone animals back to life, <i>à la</i> <em>Jurassic Park</em>. Recently, a team of scientists at Harvard University managed to insert wooly mammoth DNA into the genome of its closest relative &#8211; the Asian elephant.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/04/recreating-woolly-mammoth-dna/#more-44110" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

				<article id="post-43695">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/03/high-speed-driverless-taxi-for-the-sky/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="397" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/03/Skytran_Cityscape-007-530x397.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="Skytran_Cityscape-007" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/03/high-speed-driverless-taxi-for-the-sky/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to High-Speed Driverless Taxi for the Sky">High-Speed Driverless Taxi for the Sky</a></h2>
					<p>How do you feel when you get stuck in the traffic jam? Have you ever fantasized about escaping to another space? An innovative solution to a better way for transportation has been proposed by NASA Space Act company <a href="http://www.skytran.us/" target="_blank">skyTran</a>: an autonomous, high-speed, elevated Personal Rapid Transportation system.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/03/high-speed-driverless-taxi-for-the-sky/#more-43695" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>

			<li>
				<article id="post-43685">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/03/genetic-modification-could-prevent-tb/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="354" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/03/shutterstock_158083589-530x354.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="shutterstock_158083589" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/03/genetic-modification-could-prevent-tb/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Genetic Modification Could Prevent TB">Genetic Modification Could Prevent TB</a></h2>
					<p>Tuberculosis might sound like a thing of the past but it is still a serious problem, causing <a href="http://www.who.int/mediacentre/news/notes/2014/global-tuberculosis-report/en/" target="_blank">an estimated 1.3 &#8211; 1.5 million deaths in 2013 alone</a>. The main root of tuberculosis is infected cattle, which is transferred to humans via <a href="http://www.cdc.gov/tb/publications/factsheets/general/mbovis.pdf" target="_blank">consumption of unpasteurized dairy products</a>. However, it has recently been announced that genetic modification allowed scientists to produce cattle resistant to tuberculosis.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/03/genetic-modification-could-prevent-tb/#more-43685" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

			<li>
				<article id="post-42768">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/03/diseases-of-the-future/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="372" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/03/shutterstock_124807459-530x372.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="shutterstock_124807459" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/03/diseases-of-the-future/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Diseases Of The Future">Diseases Of The Future</a></h2>
					<p>Nowadays humans suffer from diseases that didn&#8217;t exist in the past, a trend that will probably continue into the future. A wide range of new disorders, especially related to the latest technologies, may affect us.</p>
<p>The disease of the future are related to our modern lifestyle, they affect the psyche but, in the long run, can also debilitate the organism. Computers, video games, office work, virtual realities, and their lumbering presence, are just some of the elements that have changed the context in which we live and the way we spend our time. Technology has found our new weaknesses and will exploit them.</p>
<p>Even if it&#8217;s impossible to know which pathogens will afflict us in the future, we can explore the health issues that could emerge as a consequence of technological advancements and our inability to cope with them. Virtual Reality Addiction, Nature Deficit Disorder, Computerization of the Personality, Nanotech Poisoning, shown below a selection of third millennium diseases.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/03/diseases-of-the-future/#more-42768" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

				<article id="post-42826">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/02/interview-bruce-sterling-on-the-convergence-of-humans-and-machines/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="353" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/o-BRUCE-STERLING-facebook-530x353.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="o-BRUCE-STERLING-facebook" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/02/interview-bruce-sterling-on-the-convergence-of-humans-and-machines/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Interview: Bruce Sterling on the Convergence of Humans and Machines">Interview: Bruce Sterling on the Convergence of Humans and Machines</a></h2>
					<p>Bruce Sterling is a prominent science fiction writer and a pioneer of the cyberpunk genre. His cyberpunk novels <em>Heavy Weather</em> (1994), <em>Islands in the Net</em> (1988), <em>Schismatrix</em> (1985), <em>The Artificial Kid</em> (1980) earned him the nickname “Chairman Bruce”. Apart from his writings, Bruce Sterling is also a professor of internet studies and science fiction at the European Graduate School. He has contributed to several projects within the scheme of futurist theory, founded an environmental aesthetic movement, edited anthologies and he still continues to write for several magazines including Wired, Discover, Architectural Record and The Atlantic.</p>
<p>In the interview below, we had the honor of hosting Bruce Sterling in our Next Nature Network headquarters to talk to him about the concept of the convergence of humans and machines. Sterling weighs in on the issue with a rather challenging perspective.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/02/interview-bruce-sterling-on-the-convergence-of-humans-and-machines/#more-42826" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

			<li>
				<article id="post-42809">
					<span class="vvqbox vvqyoutube" style="width:530px;height:324px;"><span id="vvq-42809-youtube-1"><a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=guh7i7tHeZk"><img src="http://img.youtube.com/vi/guh7i7tHeZk/0.jpg" alt="YouTube Preview Image" /></a></span></span>					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/02/what-if-humans-disappeared/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to What if Humans Disappeared?">What if Humans Disappeared?</a></h2>
					
<p>Life would normally continue with humans and their evolving surroundings, but this movie envisions what could happen if we would just disappear.</p>
<p><span style="line-height: 1.5em;">Humanity made a strong impact on the planet, but we should not underestimate the incredible power of nature. With our disappearance, a</span><span style="line-height: 1.5em;">nimals that depend on us will suffer drastic population declines. At the same time, without human presence on Earth, some animal species that are close to extinction would suddenly grow in population. Most of our remains will decompose because of nature power initiated by fire, weeds and termites. The only thing that would remain of us would be our trash of plastic, chemicals and radioactive material. </span><span style="line-height: 1.5em;">But of course the question is, why would we all of a sudden disappear?</span></p>
<p style="text-align: left;" align="right">Source<i>:</i> <a href="https://www.youtube.com/user/AsapSCIENCE">Asap SCIENCE</a></p>

			<li>
				<article id="post-42509">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/01/cities-evolve-in-similair-ways-as-galaxies/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="294" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/glowingplanet-530x294.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="glowingplanet" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/01/cities-evolve-in-similair-ways-as-galaxies/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Cities Evolve in Similar Ways as Galaxies">Cities Evolve in Similar Ways as Galaxies</a></h2>
					<p data-article-id="328701" data-thread-id="149102" data-annotation-count="0">Satellite images of Earth at night evoke ambiguous feelings: While on a ground level our cities appear as purely cultural artifacts, a traveler from outer space might just as well marvel at them as beautifully <em>glowing</em> <em>organic fungi-like structures</em> that sprouted on our planet. Less than a millennium ago, the Earth at night was all dark. Today it is all glowing and blossoming.</p>
<p data-article-id="328701" data-thread-id="149102" data-annotation-count="0">Scientists think the laws governing the structure of galaxies in outer space are the same laws underlying the growth of cities. Henry Lin and Abraham Loeb at the Harvard-Smithsonian Centre for Astrophysics have used models for showing how galaxies evolve based on matter density to <a href="http://www.technologyreview.com/view/534251/astrophysicists-prove-that-cities-on-earth-grow-in-the-same-way-as-galaxies-in-space/?utm_campaign=socialsync&amp;utm_medium=social-post&amp;utm_source=facebook" target="_blank">propose a unifying theory for scaling laws</a> of human populations.</p>
<p data-article-id="328701" data-thread-id="149103" data-annotation-count="0"> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/01/cities-evolve-in-similair-ways-as-galaxies/#more-42509" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>
				</article>

					<div class="meta-author">

</a>

					<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/01/cities-evolve-in-similair-ways-as-galaxies/#comments" class="nr-of-comments"  title="Comment on Cities Evolve in Similar Ways as Galaxies">1 Comment &raquo;</a>					</div>

				<article id="post-42338">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/01/bio-art-design-awards-2015/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="287" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/B-530x287.png" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="B" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/01/bio-art-design-awards-2015/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Bio Art &amp; Design Awards 2015">Bio Art &#038; Design Awards 2015</a></h2>
					<p>So, you are well aware that <a title="how  biotech will drive our evolution" href="http://www.nextnature.net/2010/08//?p=3407">biotech will drive our evolution</a>, you took the <a title="crash course on synthetic genomics" href="http://www.nextnature.net/2010/08//?p=3759">crash course on synthetic genomics</a>, you’ve got your <a title="mapping the DNA world" href="http://www.nextnature.net/2010/08/?p=3929">map of the DNA world</a> in your backpack and are now eager to redesign some microbes that <a title="bacteria that eat waste and shit petrol" href="http://www.nextnature.net/2010/08/2008/12/bacteria-that-eat-waste-shit-petrol/">turn waste into energy</a>, <a title="designing bugs that eat plastic" href="http://www.nextnature.net/2010/08/2009/12/designing-the-bugs-that-eat-plastic/">eat plastic</a>, <a title="FluDOC" href="http://nextnature.net/2010/05/fludoc-glowing-bacteria-tell-if-you-have-flue/" target="_blank">detect flu</a>, or <a title="build a better  being" href="http://www.nextnature.net/2010/08/?p=2538">build a better being</a> altogether? You have a brilliant project plan already, but only need some – let say– euro 25.000 and a bit of help from a research group to turn your vision into reality? We have cake for you.</p>
<p> <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2015/01/bio-art-design-awards-2015/#more-42338" class="more-link">Read more &raquo;</a></p>

			<li>
				<article id="post-42077">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/12/blaming-car-technology-for-dumb-drivers/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="298" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2014/12/cars-530x298.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="cars" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/12/blaming-car-technology-for-dumb-drivers/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Blaming Car Technology for Dumb Drivers">Blaming Car Technology for Dumb Drivers</a></h2>
					<p>We increasingly depend on car technology designed to make driving easier and safer. Therefore, can be said that these improvements are creating less-skilled drivers?</p>
<p><em>“Technological crutches like GPS are making us not only worse drivers – they could also be making us stupid. </em><em>Technology wasn’t supposed to work that way. Manufacturers have supported drivers with power steering, cruise control, antilock brakes and electronic stability controls. Then they gave us sophisticated on-board computers that power car entertainment systems and fine-tune our cars’ performance on the go. Today we drive sleek, aerodynamic vehicles with more computing power than early Space Shuttles.”<br />
</em><br />
We&#8217;ve already seen GPS lead people into some <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2008/03/find-brain-replace-with-gps/" target="_blank">ridiculous situations</a>.<br />
But can we blame the GPS for this, when we follow directions that are totally contrary to good sense?</p>
<p>Read more on <a href="http://www.bbc.com/future/story/20141119-is-tech-creating-stupid-drivers" target="_blank">BBC Future</a></p>
				</article>

					<p>If you happen to be in New York City this week, you may want to join us for <a href="http://www.biofabricate.co/" target="_blank">BIOFABRICATE</a>, the world’s first summit dedicated to biofabrication for future industrial and consumer products.</p>

			<li>
				<article id="post-41736">
										<a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/11/reinventing-nature-with-synthetic-biology/" rel="bookmark"><img width="530" height="365" src="http://www.nextnature.net/wp-content/uploads/2014/11/natures-technician-530x365.jpg" class="attachment-large wp-post-image" alt="natures-technician" /></a>
					<h2><a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2014/11/reinventing-nature-with-synthetic-biology/" rel="bookmark" title="Permanent Link to Reinventing Nature with Synthetic Biology">Reinventing Nature with Synthetic Biology</a></h2>
					<p>Bioengineer Drew Endy shares his idea of biology as a precision manufacturer that could potentially transform civilization as we know it.</p>
<p><em>&#8220;There is this natural technology out there in the wild that is so capable of manufacturing stuff that it coats the surface of the Earth. It takes atoms from the atmosphere and light from the environment and self-assembles huge structures with atomic precision.&#8221;</em></p>
<p>According to Endy the only option we have is to embrace a synthetic biological future, to change the way we live, manufacture and consume. <em>“We are destroying environments, we are critically ripping away biodiversity; it’s a disaster” </em>he states<em>. “We actually have a chance of reinventing civilization”.</em></p>
<p>Read more on <a href="http://discovermagazine.com/2014/oct/17-natures-technician" target="_blank">Discover Magazione<br />
</a>Related post: <a href="http://www.nextnature.net/2013/05/the-prefuture-of-synthetic-biology/" target="_blank">The Prefuture of Synthetic Biology</a></p>
				</article>
